# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Implement RateLimitMiddleware for Django

## Objective
Create a new `RateLimitMiddleware` class in `django/middleware/ratelimit.py` that provides
configurable per-IP request rate limiting using Django's cache framework.

## Requirements

1. **Create `django/middleware/ratelimit.py`** with a `RateLimitMiddleware` class that:
   - Inherits from `MiddlewareMixin` (see `django/utils/deprecation.py`)
   - Reads configuration from `settings.RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS` (default: 100) and `settings.RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW` (default: 3600 seconds)
   - Uses Django's cache framework (`django.core.cache.cache`) to track request counts per IP
   - Returns `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` (429) when limit is exceeded
   - Implements `process_request(self, request)` following the middleware pattern

2. **Update `django/http/__init__.py`** to export `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` if not already present

3. **Create `tests/middleware/test_ratelimit.py`** with test cases for:
   - Normal requests within limit
   - Requests exceeding limit
   - Cache key isolation per IP
   - Custom settings override

## Key Reference Files
- `django/middleware/csrf.py` — middleware pattern with `process_request`/`process_view`
- `django/middleware/common.py` — middleware using settings and returning responses
- `django/utils/deprecation.py` — `MiddlewareMixin` base class
- `django/core/cache/__init__.py` — cache framework API
- `django/http/response.py` — HTTP response classes (HttpResponseForbidden, etc.)

## Success Criteria
- RateLimitMiddleware class exists and follows Django middleware conventions
- Uses cache framework for rate tracking (not in-memory dict)
- Returns 429 status code when rate limit exceeded
- Has proper imports from django.conf, django.core.cache, django.http
- Test file exists with JUnit-style test methods

     1→from django.conf import settings
     2→from django.core.cache import cache
     3→from django.http import HttpResponseTooManyRequests
     4→from django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin
     5→
     6→
     7→class RateLimitMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):
     8→    """
     9→    Middleware for rate limiting requests based on client IP address.
    10→
    11→    Uses Django's cache framework to track the number of requests per IP
    12→    and returns a 429 (Too Many Requests) response when the limit is exceeded.
    13→
    14→    Configuration via settings:
    15→    - RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS: Maximum number of requests per window (default: 100)
    16→    - RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)
    17→    """
    18→
    19→    def process_request(self, request):
    20→        """
    21→        Check if the client IP has exceeded the rate limit.
    22→        Returns a 429 response if the limit is exceeded.
    23→        """
    24→        # Get the client IP address from the request
    25→        client_ip = self.get_client_ip(request)
    26→
    27→        # Get configuration from settings with defaults
    28→        rate_limit_requests = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS', 100)
    29→        rate_limit_window = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW', 3600)
    30→
    31→        # Create a cache key for this IP
    32→        cache_key = f'rate_limit:{client_ip}'
    33→
    34→        # Get the current request count from cache
    35→        request_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)
    36→
    37→        # Check if the limit has been exceeded
    38→        if request_count >= rate_limit_requests:
    39→            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()
    40→
    41→        # Increment the request count
    42→        
... (truncated)

# RateLimitMiddleware Implementation Summary

## Files Created

### 1. django/middleware/ratelimit.py
- **Class**: RateLimitMiddleware
- **Base Class**: MiddlewareMixin
- **Key Methods**:
  - `process_request(request)`: Checks rate limit and returns 429 if exceeded
  - `get_client_ip(request)`: Extracts client IP from request (supports X-Forwarded-For)
- **Configuration**:
  - `RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS`: Max requests per window (default: 100)
  - `RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW`: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)
- **Cache Key Format**: `rate_limit:{client_ip}`

### 2. tests/middleware/test_ratelimit.py
- **Test Class**: RateLimitMiddlewareTests
- **Test Cases**:
  1. Normal requests within limit
  2. Multiple requests within limit
  3. Requests exceeding limit (returns 429)
  4. Cache key isolation per IP
  5. X-Forwarded-For header support
  6. Default settings
  7. IP extraction from REMOTE_ADDR
  8. IP extraction from X-Forwarded-For
  9. Whitespace handling in X-Forwarded-For
  10. Cache key uniqueness per IP
  11. Cache increment on first request

- Fixed Python 3.10 compatibility: datetime.UTC → datetime.timezone.utc

### 4. django/utils/http.py
- Fixed Python 3.10 compatibility: datetime.UTC → datetime.timezone.utc (2 occurrences)

## Summary of Implementation

I have successfully implemented the `RateLimitMiddleware` for Django with complete test coverage. Here's what was created:

### **Files Created:**

1. **`django/middleware/ratelimit.py`** - RateLimitMiddleware class
   - Inherits from `MiddlewareMixin`
   - Implements `process_request()` method for rate limiting
   - Uses Django's cache framework to track per-IP request counts
   - Returns `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` (429) when limit is exceeded
   - Supports configurable limits via settings:
     - `RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS` (default: 100)
     - `RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW` (default: 3600 seconds)
   - Includes `get_client_ip()` helper that handles X-Forwarded-For headers

2. **`tests/middleware/test_ratelimit.py`** - Comprehensive test suite
   - **11 test cases** covering:
     - Normal requests within limit
     - Multiple requests from same IP
     - Requests exceeding limit (429 response)
     - Cache key isolation per IP
     - X-Forwarded-For header handling
     - Custom settings override
     - IP extraction logic
     - Cache behavior verification

### **Files Modified:**

1. **`django/http/__init__.py`** - Added export for `HttpResponseTooManyRequests`
2. **`django/http/response.py`** - Added `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` class with status code 429
3. **`django/utils/version.py`** - Fixed Python 3.10 compatibility
4. **`django/utils/http.py`** - Fixed Python 3.10 compatibility

✅ Per-IP rate limiting using cache framework  
✅ Supports proxied requests (X-Forwarded-For)  
✅ Fully configurable limits and windows  
✅ Proper cache key isolation  
✅ Follows Django middleware conventions  
✅ Comprehensive test coverage (11 test cases)

RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS: Maximum number of requests per window (default: 100)\n    - RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def process_request(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Check if the client IP has exceeded the rate limit.\n        Returns a 429 response if the limit is exceeded.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Get the client IP address from the request\n        client_ip = self.get_client_ip(request)\n\n        # Get configuration from settings with defaults\n        rate_limit_requests = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS', 100)\n        rate_limit_window = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW', 3600)\n\n        # Create a cache key for this IP\n        cache_key = f'rate_limit:{client_ip}'\n\n        # Get the current request count from cache\n        request_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)\n\n        # Check if the limit has been exceeded\n        if request_count >= rate_limit_requests:\n            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()\n\n        # Increment the request count\n        cache.set(cache_key, request_count + 1, rate_limit_window)\n\n        return None\n\n    def get_client_ip(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Extract the client IP address from the request.\n\n        Checks for X-Forwarded-For header first (for proxied requests),\n        then falls back to REMOTE_ADDR.\n        \"\"\"\n        x_forwarded_for = request.META.get('HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR')\n        if x_forwarded_for:\n            # X-Forwarded-For can contain multiple IPs; use the first one\n            ip = x_forwarded_for.split(',')[0].strip()\n            return ip\n        return request.META.get('REMOTE_ADDR', '')\n",

Make 10 requests (default limit is 100)\n        for _ in range(10):\n            response = self.middleware.process_request(request)\n            self.assertIsNone(response)\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=5, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)\n    def test_request_exceeding_limit(self):\n        \"\"\"Requests exceeding the limit should return 429.\"\"\"\n        request = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='127.0.0.1')\n\n        # Make 5 requests (the limit)\n        for _ in range(5):\n            response = self.middleware.process_request(request)\n            self.assertIsNone(response)\n\n        # The 6th request should be blocked\n        response = self.middleware.process_request(request)\n        self.assertIsNotNone(response)\n        self.assertIsInstance(response, HttpResponseTooManyRequests)\n        self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 429)\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=3, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)\n    def test_different_ips_isolated(self):\n        \"\"\"Different IPs should have separate rate limits.\"\"\"\n        # Make 3 requests from IP 1\n        request1 = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='192.168.1.1')\n        for _ in range(3):\n            response = self.middleware.process_request(request1)\n            self.assertIsNone(response)\n\n        # The 4th request from IP 1 should be blocked\n        response = self.middleware.process_request(request1)\n        self.assertIsInstance(response, HttpResponseTooManyRequests)\n\n        # But IP 2 should still be able to make requests\n        request2 = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='192.168.1.2')\n        response = self.middleware.process_request(request2)\n        self.assertIsNone(response)\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=2, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)\n    def test_x_forwarded_for_header(self):\n        \"\"\"IP should be extracted from X-Forwarded-For header if present.\"\"\"\n        # Create request with X-Forwarded-For header\n        request = self.factory.get('/', HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR='10.0.0.1, 10.0.0.2')\n\n        # Make 2 requests\n        for _ in range(2):\n            response = self.middleware.process_request(request)\n            self.assertIsNone(response)\n\n        # The 3rd request should be blocked (limit is 2)\n        response = self.middleware.process_request(request)\n        self.assertIsInstance(response, HttpResponseTooManyRequests)\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=100)\n    def test_default_window(self):\n        \"\"\"Default window should be used when not specified in settings.\"\"\"\n        request = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='127.0.0.1')\n\n        # Make a request - should succeed\n        response = self.middleware.process_request(request)\n        self.assertIsNone(response)\n\n    def test_get_client_ip_with_remote_addr(self):\n        \"\"\"get_client_ip should return REMOTE_ADDR when X-Forwarded-For is absent.\"\"\"\n        request = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='192.168.1.100')\n        ip = self.middleware.get_client_ip(request)\n        self.assertEqual(ip, '192.168.1.100')\n\n    def test_get_client_ip_with_x_forwarded_for(self):\n        \"\"\"get_client_ip should return first IP from X-Forwarded-For.\"\"\"\n        request = self.factory.get('/', HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR='203.0.113.1, 203.0.113.2')\n        ip = self.middleware.get_client_ip(request)\n        self.assertEqual(ip, '203.0.113.1')\n\n    def test_get_client_ip_with_whitespace(self):\n        \"\"\"get_client_ip should handle whitespace in X-Forwarded-For.\"\"\"\n        request = self.factory.get('/', HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR='203.0.113.1  ,  203.0.113.2')\n        ip = self.middleware.get_client_ip(request)\n        self.assertEqual(ip, '203.0.113.1')\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=2, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)\n    def test_cache_key_isolation(self):\n        \"\"\"Cache keys should be unique per IP.\"\"\"\n        request1 = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='192.168.1.1')\n        request2 = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='192.168.1.2')\n\n        # Make requests from both IPs\n        self.middleware.process_request(request1)\n        self.middleware.process_request(request2)\n\n        # Verify cache keys are different\n        cache_key1 = 'rate_limit:192.168.1.1'\n        cache_key2 = 'rate_limit:192.168.1.2'\n\n        count1 = cache.get(cache_key1)\n        count2 = cache.get(cache_key2)\n\n        self.assertEqual(count1, 1)\n        self.assertEqual(count2, 1)\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=1, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)\n    def test_first_request_incremented(self):\n        \"\"\"First request should increment cache to 1.\"\"\"\n        request = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='127.0.0.1')\n        self.middleware.process_request(request)\n\n        cache_key = 'rate_limit:127.0.0.1'\n        count = cache.get(cache_key)\n        self.assertEqual(count, 1)\n",

If count >= RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS, returns HttpResponseTooManyRequests (429)\n5. Otherwise, increments count in cache with TTL = RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW\n6. Returns None to continue processing\n\n### Key Features\n- Per-IP rate limiting using Django's cache framework\n- Supports proxied requests via X-Forwarded-For header\n- Configurable limits and time windows\n- Proper cache key isolation per IP\n- Clean, maintainable code following Django patterns\n\n## Test Coverage\n- 11 comprehensive test cases covering:\n  - Basic functionality (requests within/exceeding limit)\n  - Configuration override via @override_settings\n  - IP extraction methods\n  - Cache behavior\n  - X-Forwarded-For header handling\n  - Edge cases (whitespace in headers, missing headers)\nEOF\ncat /tmp/implementation_summary.md\n",

5. WRITE /workspace/django/middleware/ratelimit.py
from django.conf import settings
from django.core.cache import cache
from django.http import HttpResponseTooManyRequests
from django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin


class RateLimitMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):
    """
    Middleware for rate limiting requests based on client IP address.

    Uses Django's cache framework to track the number of requests per IP
    and returns a 429 (Too Many Requests) response when the limit is exceeded.

    Configuration via settings:
    - RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS: Maximum number of requests per window (default: 100)
    - RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)
    """

    def process_request(self, request):
        """
        Check if the client IP has exceeded the rate limit.
        Returns a 429 response if the limit is exceeded.
        """
        # Get the client IP address from the request
        client_ip = self.get_client_ip(request)

        # Get configuration from settings with defaults
        rate_limit_requests = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS', 100)
        rate_limit_window = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW', 3600)

        # Create a cache key for this IP
        cache_key = f'rate_limit:{client_ip}'

        # Get the current request count from cache
        request_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)

        # Check if the limit has been exceeded
        if request_count >= rate_limit_requests:
            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()

        # Increment the request count
        cache.set(cache_key, request_count + 1, rate_limit_window)

        return None

    def get_client_ip(self, request):
        """
        Extract the client IP address from the request.

        Checks for X-Forwarded-For header first (for proxied requests),
        then falls back to REMOTE_
... (truncated)

from django.core.cache import cache
from django.http import HttpResponse, HttpResponseTooManyRequests
from django.middleware.ratelimit import RateLimitMiddleware
from django.test import RequestFactory, SimpleTestCase, override_settings


def get_response(request):
    """Simple response for testing."""
    return HttpResponse()


class RateLimitMiddlewareTests(SimpleTestCase):
    """Tests for RateLimitMiddleware."""

    def setUp(self):
        """Clear cache before each test."""
        cache.clear()
        self.factory = RequestFactory()
        self.middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)

    def tearDown(self):
        """Clear cache after each test."""
        cache.clear()

    def test_normal_request_within_limit(self):
        """Requests within the limit should be allowed."""
        request = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='127.0.0.1')
        response = self.middleware.process_request(request)
        self.assertIsNone(response)

    def test_multiple_requests_within_limit(self):
        """Multiple requests from the same IP within limit should be allowed."""
        request = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='127.0.0.1')

        # Make 10 requests (default limit is 100)
        for _ in range(10):
            response = self.middleware.process_request(request)
            self.assertIsNone(response)

    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=5, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)
    def test_request_exceeding_limit(self):
        """Requests exceeding the limit should return 429."""
        request = self.factory.get('/', REMOTE_ADDR='127.0.0.1')

        # Make 5 requests (the limit)
        for _ in range(5):
            response = self.middleware.process_request(request)
            self.assertIsNone(response)

# RateLimitMiddleware Implementation Summary

## Files Created

### 1. django/middleware/ratelimit.py
- **Class**: RateLimitMiddleware
- **Base Class**: MiddlewareMixin
- **Key Methods**:
  - `process_request(request)`: Checks rate limit and returns 429 if exceeded
  - `get_client_ip(request)`: Extracts client IP from request (supports X-Forwarded-For)
- **Configuration**:
  - `RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS`: Max requests per window (default: 100)
  - `RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW`: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)
- **Cache Key Format**: `rate_limit:{client_ip}`

### 2. tests/middleware/test_ratelimit.py
- **Test Class**: RateLimitMiddlewareTests
- **Test Cases**:
  1. Normal requests within limit
  2. Multiple requests within limit
  3. Requests exceeding limit (returns 429)
  4. Cache key isolation per IP
  5. X-Forwarded-For header support
  6. Default settings
  7. IP extraction from REMOTE_ADDR
  8. IP extraction from X-Forwarded-For
  9. Whitespace handling in X-Forwarded-For
  10. Cache key uniqueness per IP
  11. Cache increment on first request

## Files Modified

### 1. django/http/__init__.py
- Added `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` to imports
- Added `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` to __all__ list

### 2. django/http/response.py
- Added `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` class (status_code = 429)
- Fixed Python 3.10 compatibility: datetime.UTC → datetime.timezone.utc

### 3. django/utils/version.py
- Fixed Python 3.10 compatibility: datetime.UTC → datetime.timezone.utc

### 4. django/utils/http.py
- Fixed Python 3.10 compatibility: datetime.UTC → datetime.timezone.utc (2 occurrences)

## Implementation Details

### RateLimitMiddleware Logic
1. Extracts client IP from request (X-Forwarded-For or REMOTE_ADDR)
2. Creates cache key: `rate_limit:{client_ip}`
3. Retrieves current request count from cache
4. If count >= RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS, returns HttpResponseTooManyRequests (429)
5. Otherwise, increments count in cache with TTL = RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW
6. Returns None to continue processing

### Key Features
- Per-IP rate limiting using Django's cache framework
- Supports proxied requests via X-Forwarded-For header
- Configurable limits and time windows
- Proper cache key isolation per IP
- Clean, maintainable code following Django patterns

## Test Coverage
- 11 comprehensive test cases covering:
  - Basic functionality (requests within/exceeding limit)
  - Configuration override via @override_settings
  - IP extraction methods
  - Cache behavior
  - X-Forwarded-For header handling
  - Edge cases (whitespace in headers, missing headers)
EOF

#!/usr/bin/env python3
import os
import sys

def check_file_exists(path, description):
    if os.path.exists(path):
        size = os.path.getsize(path)
        print(f"✓ {description}: {path} ({size} bytes)")
        return True
    else:
        print(f"✗ {description}: {path} NOT FOUND")
        return False

def check_file_contains(path, content, description):
    if not os.path.exists(path):
        print(f"✗ {description}: {path} NOT FOUND")
        return False
    with open(path, 'r') as f:
        file_content = f.read()
        if content in file_content:
            print(f"✓ {description}: Found in {path}")
            return True
        else:
            print(f"✗ {description}: NOT FOUND in {path}")
            return False

print("=" * 70)
